        <title>Draft genome sequence and detailed characterization of biofuel production by oleaginous microalga Scenedesmus quadricauda LWG002611 | Biotechnology for Biofuels | Full Text</title>

        

    <meta name="citation_abstract" content="Due to scarcity of fossil fuel, the importance of alternative energy sources is ever increasing. The oleaginous microalgae have demonstrated their potential as an alternative source of energy, but have not achieved commercialization owing to some biological and technical inefficiency. Modern methods of recombinant strain development for improved efficacy are suffering due to inadequate knowledge of genome and limited molecular tools available for their manipulation. In the present study, microalga Scenedesmus quadricauda LWG002611 was selected as the preferred organism for lipid production as it contained high biomass (0.37&#160;g&#160;L&#8722;1&#160;day&#8722;1) and lipid (102 mg&#160;L&#8722;1&#160;day&#8722;1), compared to other oleaginous algae examined in the present study as well as earlier reports. It possessed suitable biodiesel properties as per the range defined by the European biodiesel standard EN14214 and petro-diesel standard EN590:2013. To investigate the potential of S. quadricauda LWG002611 in details, the genome of the organism was assembled and annotated. This was the first genome sequencing and assembly of S. quadricauda, which predicted a genome size of 65.35&#160;Mb with 13,514 genes identified by de novo and 16,739 genes identified by reference guided annotation. Comparative genomics revealed that it belongs to class Chlorophyceae and order Sphaeropleales. Further, small subunit ribosomal RNA gene (18S rRNA) sequencing was carried out to confirm its molecular identification. S. quadricauda LWG002611 exhibited higher number of genes related to major activities compared to other potential algae reported earlier with a total of 283 genes identified in lipid metabolism. Metabolic pathways were reconstructed and multiple gene homologs responsible for carbon fixation and triacylglycerol (TAG) biosynthesis pathway were identified to further improve this potential algal strain for biofuel production by metabolic engineering approaches. Here we present the first draft genome sequence, genetic characterization and comparative evaluation of S. quadricauda LWG002611 which exhibit high biomass as well as high lipid productivity. The knowledge of genome sequence, reconstructed metabolic pathways and identification of rate-limiting steps in TAG biosynthesis pathway will strengthen the development of molecular tools towards further improving this potentially one of the major algal strains for biofuel production."/>

    (function () {
        if ( typeof window.CustomEvent === "function" ) return false;
        function CustomEvent ( event, params ) {
            params = params || { bubbles: false, cancelable: false, detail: null };
            var evt = document.createEvent( 'CustomEvent' );
            evt.initCustomEvent( event, params.bubbles, params.cancelable, params.detail );
            return evt;
        }

        CustomEvent.prototype = window.Event.prototype;

    })();

    <link rel="canonical" href="//biotechnologyforbiofuels.biomedcentral.com/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4"/>
    

        
        
        
        <meta property="og:url" content="https://biotechnologyforbiofuels.biomedcentral.com/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4"/>
        <meta property="og:type" content="article"/>
        <meta property="og:site_name" content="Biotechnology for Biofuels"/>
        <meta property="og:title" content="Draft genome sequence and detailed characterization of biofuel production by oleaginous microalga Scenedesmus quadricauda LWG002611"/>
        <meta property="og:description" content="Due to scarcity of fossil fuel, the importance of alternative energy sources is ever increasing. The oleaginous microalgae have demonstrated their potential as an alternative source of energy, but have not achieved commercialization owing to some biological and technical inefficiency. Modern methods of recombinant strain development for improved efficacy are suffering due to inadequate knowledge of genome and limited molecular tools available for their manipulation. In the present study, microalga Scenedesmus quadricauda LWG002611 was selected as the preferred organism for lipid production as it contained high biomass (0.37&amp;nbsp;g&amp;nbsp;L−1&amp;nbsp;day−1) and lipid (102 mg&amp;nbsp;L−1&amp;nbsp;day−1), compared to other oleaginous algae examined in the present study as well as earlier reports. It possessed suitable biodiesel properties as per the range defined by the European biodiesel standard EN14214 and petro-diesel standard EN590:2013. To investigate the potential of S. quadricauda LWG002611 in details, the genome of the organism was assembled and annotated. This was the first genome sequencing and assembly of S. quadricauda, which predicted a genome size of 65.35&amp;nbsp;Mb with 13,514 genes identified by de novo and 16,739 genes identified by reference guided annotation. Comparative genomics revealed that it belongs to class Chlorophyceae and order Sphaeropleales. Further, small subunit ribosomal RNA gene (18S rRNA) sequencing was carried out to confirm its molecular identification. S. quadricauda LWG002611 exhibited higher number of genes related to major activities compared to other potential algae reported earlier with a total of 283 genes identified in lipid metabolism. Metabolic pathways were reconstructed and multiple gene homologs responsible for carbon fixation and triacylglycerol (TAG) biosynthesis pathway were identified to further improve this potential algal strain for biofuel production by metabolic engineering approaches. Here we present the first draft genome sequence, genetic characterization and comparative evaluation of S. quadricauda LWG002611 which exhibit high biomass as well as high lipid productivity. The knowledge of genome sequence, reconstructed metabolic pathways and identification of rate-limiting steps in TAG biosynthesis pathway will strengthen the development of molecular tools towards further improving this potentially one of the major algal strains for biofuel production."/>
        <meta property="og:image" content="https://media.springernature.com/w200/springer-static/cover/journal/13068.jpg"/>

                    <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" data-test="abstract-sub-heading">Background</h3><p>Due to scarcity of fossil fuel, the importance of alternative energy sources is ever increasing. The oleaginous microalgae have demonstrated their potential as an alternative source of energy, but have not achieved commercialization owing to some biological and technical inefficiency. Modern methods of recombinant strain development for improved efficacy are suffering due to inadequate knowledge of genome and limited molecular tools available for their manipulation.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" data-test="abstract-sub-heading">Results</h3><p>In the present study, microalga <i>Scenedesmus quadricauda</i> LWG002611 was selected as the preferred organism for lipid production as it contained high biomass (0.37 g L<sup>−1</sup> day<sup>−1</sup>) and lipid (102 mg L<sup>−1</sup> day<sup>−1</sup>), compared to other oleaginous algae examined in the present study as well as earlier reports. It possessed suitable biodiesel properties as per the range defined by the European biodiesel standard EN14214 and petro-diesel standard EN590:2013. To investigate the potential of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 in details, the genome of the organism was assembled and annotated. This was the first genome sequencing and assembly of <i>S. quadricauda,</i> which predicted a genome size of 65.35 Mb with 13,514 genes identified by de novo and 16,739 genes identified by reference guided annotation. Comparative genomics revealed that it belongs to class Chlorophyceae and order Sphaeropleales. Further, small subunit ribosomal RNA gene (18S rRNA) sequencing was carried out to confirm its molecular identification. <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 exhibited higher number of genes related to major activities compared to other potential algae reported earlier with a total of 283 genes identified in lipid metabolism. Metabolic pathways were reconstructed and multiple gene homologs responsible for carbon fixation and triacylglycerol (TAG) biosynthesis pathway were identified to further improve this potential algal strain for biofuel production by metabolic engineering approaches.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" data-test="abstract-sub-heading">Conclusion</h3><p>Here we present the first draft genome sequence, genetic characterization and comparative evaluation of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 which exhibit high biomass as well as high lipid productivity. The knowledge of genome sequence, reconstructed metabolic pathways and identification of rate-limiting steps in TAG biosynthesis pathway will strengthen the development of molecular tools towards further improving this potentially one of the major algal strains for biofuel production.</p></div></div></section>
                    
    


                    <section aria-labelledby="Sec1" data-title="Background"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec1">Background</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec1-content"><p>The scarcity of fossil fuel as well as intricate link in climate change has necessitated the search for alternative fuel. In this context, oleaginous microalgae are in demand due to high biomass and lipid productivity as evidenced by accumulation of 40–80% TAG per gram dry weight [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Chisti Y. Biodiesel from microalgae. Biotechnol Adv. 2007;25:294–306." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d62726e504">1</a>].</p><p>Several algal strains including <i>Chlorella</i>, <i>Nannochloropsis</i>, <i>Scenedesmus, Kirchneriella</i> and <i>Selenastrum</i> have been screened for biomass and lipid productivity as they are easy to isolate, demonstrate growth robustness with high lipid content [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Demirbas MF. Biofuels from algae for sustainable development. Appl Energy. 2011;88:3473–80." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d62726e522">2</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Rawat I, Kumar RR, Mutanda T, Bux F. Biodiesel from microalgae: a critical evaluation from laboratory to large scale production. Appl Energy. 2013;103:444–67." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d62726e526">3</a>]. <i>Scenedesmus</i> comprises entire desirable characteristics in one organism including high lipid production and wide growth range under diverse condition as compared to other oleaginous microalgae [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ren HY, Liu BF, Ma C, Zhao L, Ren NQ. A new lipid-rich microalga Scenedesmus sp. strain R-16 isolated using Nile red staining: effects of carbon and nitrogen sources and initial pH on the biomass and lipid production. Biotechnol Biofuels. 2013;6(1):143." href="#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d62726e532">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Mata MT, Melo AC, Meireles S, Mendes AM, Martins AA, Caetano NS. Potential of microalgae Scenedesmus obliquus grown in brewery wastewater for biodiesel production. Chem Eng Trans. 2013;32:901–5." href="#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d62726e532_1">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wong YK, Yung KKL, Tsang YF, Xia Y, Wang L, Ho KC. Scenedesmus quadricauda for nutrient removal and lipid production in wastewater. Water Environ Res. 2015;87(12):2037–44." href="#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d62726e532_2">6</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Dasgupta CN, Suseela MR, Mandotra SK, Kumar P, Pandey MK, Toppo K, et al. Dual uses of microalgal biomass: an integrative approach for biohydrogen and biodiesel production. Appl Energy. 2015;146:202–8." href="#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d62726e532_3">7</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Knothe G. Improving biodiesel fuel properties by modifying fatty ester composition. Energy Environ Sci. 2009;2(7):759–66." href="#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d62726e532_4">8</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Rodolfi L, Chini Zittelli G, Bassi N, Padovani G, Biondi N, Bonini G, et al. Microalgae for oil: strain selection, induction of lipid synthesis and outdoor mass cultivation in a low-cost photobioreactor. Biotechnol Bioeng. 2009;102(1):100–12." href="#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d62726e532_5">9</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Sulochana SB, Arumugam M. Influence of abscisic acid on growth, biomass and lipid yield of Scenedesmus quadricauda under nitrogen starved condition. Bioresour Technol. 2016;213:198–203." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d62726e535">10</a>]. The lipid content of <i>Scenedesmus</i> varies from 10 to 50% of dry biomass according to strain and growth condition [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ren HY, Liu BF, Ma C, Zhao L, Ren NQ. A new lipid-rich microalga Scenedesmus sp. strain R-16 isolated using Nile red staining: effects of carbon and nitrogen sources and initial pH on the biomass and lipid production. Biotechnol Biofuels. 2013;6(1):143." href="#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d62726e541">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Mata MT, Melo AC, Meireles S, Mendes AM, Martins AA, Caetano NS. Potential of microalgae Scenedesmus obliquus grown in brewery wastewater for biodiesel production. Chem Eng Trans. 2013;32:901–5." href="#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d62726e541_1">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wong YK, Yung KKL, Tsang YF, Xia Y, Wang L, Ho KC. Scenedesmus quadricauda for nutrient removal and lipid production in wastewater. Water Environ Res. 2015;87(12):2037–44." href="#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d62726e541_2">6</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="Dasgupta CN, Suseela MR, Mandotra SK, Kumar P, Pandey MK, Toppo K, et al. Dual uses of microalgal biomass: an integrative approach for biohydrogen and biodiesel production. Appl Energy. 2015;146:202–8." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d62726e545">7</a>]. Out of all species, <i>S. quadricauda</i> is less exploited but could be an efficient candidate for future needs [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Mata MT, Melo AC, Meireles S, Mendes AM, Martins AA, Caetano NS. Potential of microalgae Scenedesmus obliquus grown in brewery wastewater for biodiesel production. Chem Eng Trans. 2013;32:901–5." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d62726e551">5</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Rodolfi L, Chini Zittelli G, Bassi N, Padovani G, Biondi N, Bonini G, et al. Microalgae for oil: strain selection, induction of lipid synthesis and outdoor mass cultivation in a low-cost photobioreactor. Biotechnol Bioeng. 2009;102(1):100–12." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d62726e554">9</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Sulochana SB, Arumugam M. Influence of abscisic acid on growth, biomass and lipid yield of Scenedesmus quadricauda under nitrogen starved condition. Bioresour Technol. 2016;213:198–203." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d62726e557">10</a>] as it produces ~ 50% lipid (weight/weight) of dry biomass [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Mata MT, Melo AC, Meireles S, Mendes AM, Martins AA, Caetano NS. Potential of microalgae Scenedesmus obliquus grown in brewery wastewater for biodiesel production. Chem Eng Trans. 2013;32:901–5." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d62726e560">5</a>] with desired quantity of saturated and unsaturated C16 and C18 fatty acids, which is a must for efficient biodiesel production [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Knothe G. Improving biodiesel fuel properties by modifying fatty ester composition. Energy Environ Sci. 2009;2(7):759–66." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d62726e564">8</a>].</p><p>In the present scenario, the maximum global microalgal biofuel productivity (when substrates are sufficient and conditions are within the optimal growth range) is estimated to be 3.2–14.8 TOE (tonnes of oil equivalent) ha<sup>−1</sup> year<sup>−1</sup> with a global average of 8.4 TOE ha<sup>−1</sup> year<sup>−1</sup> (in open ponds with 25% lipid content) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Park H, Lee C. Theoretical calculations on the feasibility of microalgal biofuels: utilization of marine resources could help realizing the potential of microalgae. Biotechnol J. 2016;11(11):1461–70." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d62726e578">11</a>]. An exceptionally high algal biofuel yield prediction of ~ 136.9 TOE ha<sup>−1</sup> year<sup>−1</sup> was reported by Chisti [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Chisti Y. Biodiesel from microalgae. Biotechnol Adv. 2007;25:294–306." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d62726e586">1</a>]; that is difficult to achieve in outdoor cultivation [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Abomohra AEF, Wagner M, El-Sheekh M, Hanelt D. Lipid and total fatty acid productivity in photoautotrophic fresh water microalgae: screening studies towards biodiesel production. J Appl Phycol. 2013;25:931–6." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d62726e589">12</a>]. A wide range of prices from 1.3 to 20 USD L<sup>−1</sup> have been reported for algal biofuel [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Davis R, Aden A, Pienkos PT. Techno-economic analysis of autotrophic microalgae for fuel production. Appl Energy. 2011;88:3524–31." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d62726e594">13</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Zhang Y, Liu X, White MA, Colosi LM. Economic evaluation of algae biodiesel based on meta-analyses. Int J Sustain Energy. 2017;36(7):682–94." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d62726e598">14</a>]; thus demonstrating that algal biofuel is not yet cost competitive with petroleum based fuels or other biofuels [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Shurin JB, Burkart MD, Mayfield SP, Smith VH. Recent progress and future challenges in algal biofuel production. F1000Res. 2016; e5." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d62726e601">15</a>]. However, scalability of the process is gearing up to meet sustainability [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Subhadra B. Algal biorefinery-based industry: an approach to address fuel and food insecurity for a carbon-smart world. J Sci Food Agric. 2011;91(1):2–13." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d62726e604">16</a>].</p><p>The production of algal biofuel has several advantages such as utilizing nonfood-based feedstock, utilization of non-arable land for its cultivation and can potentially utilize a wide variety of water resources including wastewater and seawater [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Demirbas MF. Biofuels from algae for sustainable development. Appl Energy. 2011;88:3473–80." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d62726e610">2</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Rawat I, Kumar RR, Mutanda T, Bux F. Biodiesel from microalgae: a critical evaluation from laboratory to large scale production. Appl Energy. 2013;103:444–67." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d62726e613">3</a>]. However, a major hurdle for this process is to achieve desired quantity of biomass and lipid content simultaneously. Most of the studies used nutrient deprivation and stress for culturing algae to induce more lipid production, but end up reducing the growth rate, thus affecting biomass productivity [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Knothe G. Improving biodiesel fuel properties by modifying fatty ester composition. Energy Environ Sci. 2009;2(7):759–66." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d62726e616">8</a>].</p><p>The identification of super productive strain is one potential solution which concomitantly with targeted metabolic engineering approaches can be applied to enhance the quantity of desired fatty acids to improve biodiesel quality, thus overcoming biological inefficiency of strain [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Knothe G. Improving biodiesel fuel properties by modifying fatty ester composition. Energy Environ Sci. 2009;2(7):759–66." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d62726e623">8</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Vieler A, Wu G, Tsai CH, Bullard B, Cornish AJ, Harvey C, et al. Genome, functional gene annotation, and nuclear transformation of the heterokont oleaginous alga Nannochloropsis oceanica CCMP1779. PLoS Genet. 2012;8(11):e1003064." href="#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d62726e626">17</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Radakovits R, Jinkerson RE, Fuerstenberg SI, Tae H, Settlage RE, Boore JL, et al. Draft genome sequence and genetic transformation of the oleaginous alga Nannochloropsis gaditana. Nat Commun. 2012;3:e686." href="#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d62726e626_1">18</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ota S, Oshima K, Yamazaki T, Kim S, Yu Z, Yoshihara M, et al. Highly efficient lipid production in the green alga Parachlorella kessleri: draft genome and transcriptome endorsed by whole-cell 3D ultrastructure. Biotechnol Biofuels. 2016;9(1):13." href="#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d62726e626_2">19</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Lin H, Miller ML, Granas DM, Dutcher SK. Whole genome sequencing identifies a deletion in protein phosphatase 2A that affects its stability and localization in Chlamydomonas reinhardtii. PLoS Genet. 2013;9(9):e1003841." href="#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d62726e626_3">20</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Merchant SS, Prochnik SE, Vallon O, Harris EH, Karpowicz SJ, Witman GB, et al. The Chlamydomonas genome reveals the evolution of key animal and plant functions. Science. 2007;318(5848):245–50." href="#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d62726e626_4">21</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Bogen C, Al-Dilaimi A, Albersmeier A, Wichmann J, Grundmann M, Rupp O, et al. Reconstruction of the lipid metabolism for the microalga Monoraphidium neglectum from its genome sequence reveals characteristics suitable for biofuel production. BMC Genomics. 2013;14(1):e926." href="#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d62726e626_5">22</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Carreres BM, de Jaeger L, Springer J, Barbosa MJ, Breuer G, van den End EJ, et al. Draft genome sequence of the oleaginous green alga Tetradesmus obliquus UTEX 393. Genome Announc. 2017;5(3):e01449-16." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d62726e629">23</a>]. However, recombinant strain development enhancing biofuel production is suffering due to lack of adequate knowledge of its genome and limited molecular manipulating tools [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Vieler A, Wu G, Tsai CH, Bullard B, Cornish AJ, Harvey C, et al. Genome, functional gene annotation, and nuclear transformation of the heterokont oleaginous alga Nannochloropsis oceanica CCMP1779. PLoS Genet. 2012;8(11):e1003064." href="#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d62726e632">17</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Radakovits R, Jinkerson RE, Fuerstenberg SI, Tae H, Settlage RE, Boore JL, et al. Draft genome sequence and genetic transformation of the oleaginous alga Nannochloropsis gaditana. Nat Commun. 2012;3:e686." href="#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d62726e632_1">18</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ota S, Oshima K, Yamazaki T, Kim S, Yu Z, Yoshihara M, et al. Highly efficient lipid production in the green alga Parachlorella kessleri: draft genome and transcriptome endorsed by whole-cell 3D ultrastructure. Biotechnol Biofuels. 2016;9(1):13." href="#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d62726e632_2">19</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Lin H, Miller ML, Granas DM, Dutcher SK. Whole genome sequencing identifies a deletion in protein phosphatase 2A that affects its stability and localization in Chlamydomonas reinhardtii. PLoS Genet. 2013;9(9):e1003841." href="#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d62726e632_3">20</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Merchant SS, Prochnik SE, Vallon O, Harris EH, Karpowicz SJ, Witman GB, et al. The Chlamydomonas genome reveals the evolution of key animal and plant functions. Science. 2007;318(5848):245–50." href="#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d62726e632_4">21</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Bogen C, Al-Dilaimi A, Albersmeier A, Wichmann J, Grundmann M, Rupp O, et al. Reconstruction of the lipid metabolism for the microalga Monoraphidium neglectum from its genome sequence reveals characteristics suitable for biofuel production. BMC Genomics. 2013;14(1):e926." href="#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d62726e632_5">22</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Carreres BM, de Jaeger L, Springer J, Barbosa MJ, Breuer G, van den End EJ, et al. Draft genome sequence of the oleaginous green alga Tetradesmus obliquus UTEX 393. Genome Announc. 2017;5(3):e01449-16." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d62726e635">23</a>]. One of the best examples is <i>Chlamydomonas reinhardtii</i> which has undergone extensive genetic manipulation because of availability of its genome sequence [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Lin H, Miller ML, Granas DM, Dutcher SK. Whole genome sequencing identifies a deletion in protein phosphatase 2A that affects its stability and localization in Chlamydomonas reinhardtii. PLoS Genet. 2013;9(9):e1003841." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d62726e642">20</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Merchant SS, Prochnik SE, Vallon O, Harris EH, Karpowicz SJ, Witman GB, et al. The Chlamydomonas genome reveals the evolution of key animal and plant functions. Science. 2007;318(5848):245–50." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d62726e645">21</a>]. In this context, genome of <i>Nannochloropsis oceanica</i>, <i>Nannochloropsis gaditana</i>, <i>Monoraphidium neglectum</i> and <i>Tetradesmus obliquus</i> were sequenced to identify the lipid biosynthetic pathways and their suitability for biofuel production [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Vieler A, Wu G, Tsai CH, Bullard B, Cornish AJ, Harvey C, et al. Genome, functional gene annotation, and nuclear transformation of the heterokont oleaginous alga Nannochloropsis oceanica CCMP1779. PLoS Genet. 2012;8(11):e1003064." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d62726e661">17</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Radakovits R, Jinkerson RE, Fuerstenberg SI, Tae H, Settlage RE, Boore JL, et al. Draft genome sequence and genetic transformation of the oleaginous alga Nannochloropsis gaditana. Nat Commun. 2012;3:e686." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d62726e664">18</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Bogen C, Al-Dilaimi A, Albersmeier A, Wichmann J, Grundmann M, Rupp O, et al. Reconstruction of the lipid metabolism for the microalga Monoraphidium neglectum from its genome sequence reveals characteristics suitable for biofuel production. BMC Genomics. 2013;14(1):e926." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d62726e667">22</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Carreres BM, de Jaeger L, Springer J, Barbosa MJ, Breuer G, van den End EJ, et al. Draft genome sequence of the oleaginous green alga Tetradesmus obliquus UTEX 393. Genome Announc. 2017;5(3):e01449-16." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d62726e670">23</a>]. However, neither of these algae is found to be an exceptional producer of biomass or lipid. With few exceptions, average microalgal biomass productivity ranges from 0.02 to 0.40 g L<sup>−1</sup> day<sup>−1</sup> and lipid productivity ranges from 5 to 178 mg L<sup>−1</sup> day<sup>−1</sup>. None of the algae has been commercialized for biodiesel production despite years of extensive efforts in research [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Shurin JB, Burkart MD, Mayfield SP, Smith VH. Recent progress and future challenges in algal biofuel production. F1000Res. 2016; e5." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d62726e682">15</a>].</p><p>In the present study, we have investigated <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611as a potential strain for biomass and lipid production. Furthermore, we have genetically characterized the strain followed by draft assembly for comparative genomics, identified functional genes and reconstructed important metabolic pathways. This is the first report on genome sequencing of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611. Based on the sequence, we have identified gene homologs of key enzymes involved in carbon fixation and TAG biosynthesis pathways, which can be targeted for genetic and metabolic engineering to further improvement of the strain.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec2" data-title="Results and discussion"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec2-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec2">Results and discussion</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec2-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec3">Selection of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 as preferred organism for biodiesel production</h3><p><i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 was found to be the most efficient strain for biomass and lipid production under both autotrophic and mixotrophic growth condition when compared to other species of <i>Scenedesmus</i> (<i>S. obliquus</i>, <i>S. dimorphus</i>, <i>S. abundans</i>) as well as other oleaginous microalgal isolates (<i>Chlorella vulgaris, Nannochloropsis oculata, Kirchneriella obesa, Chlamydomonas globosa</i>, <i>Sphaerocystis schroeteri</i>). It grew faster in mixotrophic growth condition (supplemented with 17.4 mM acetate in TAP medium) than autotrophic condition (in BBM) and achieved stationary growth phase within 8 days of culture. The maximum biomass productivity (0.37 g L<sup>−1</sup> day<sup>−1</sup>) achieved by <i>S. quadricauda</i> in TAP medium; which was 27.5% more than the biomass productivity (0.29  g L<sup>−1</sup> day<sup>−1</sup>) achieved in BBM in exponential phase of growth (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig1">1</a>a). After 25 days of growth, biomass of all isolates were harvested and lyophilized and total biomass yield was estimated. <i>Scenedesmus, Nannochloropsis</i> and <i>Chlorella</i> were found to be the highest biomass yielding isolates. However, the maximum biomass content of 1.41 g L<sup>−1</sup> was achieved by <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 followed by 1.29 g L<sup>−1</sup> achieved by <i>N. oculata</i> in TAP medium. As expected, highest lipid productivity was observed in <i>S. quadricauda</i> (102 mg L<sup>−1</sup> day<sup>−1</sup>) in TAP media followed by <i>S. obliquus</i> (67 mg L<sup>−1</sup> day<sup>−1</sup>) without any starvation (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig1">1</a>b). The total lipid content of 404 mg L<sup>−1</sup> was achieved by <i>S. quadricauda</i> in TAP medium without nitrogen deprivation or any other starvation. This study mirrors what has been found earlier that additions of organic carbon (acetate) boosted up total carbon assimilation of algae and helped to improve biomass as well as lipid production [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="Dasgupta CN, Suseela MR, Mandotra SK, Kumar P, Pandey MK, Toppo K, et al. Dual uses of microalgal biomass: an integrative approach for biohydrogen and biodiesel production. Appl Energy. 2015;146:202–8." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d62726e786">7</a>]. It produced 1.9-fold more biomass and 2.9-fold more lipid than the <i>S. quadricauda</i> as screened by Rodolfi et al. [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Rodolfi L, Chini Zittelli G, Bassi N, Padovani G, Biondi N, Bonini G, et al. Microalgae for oil: strain selection, induction of lipid synthesis and outdoor mass cultivation in a low-cost photobioreactor. Biotechnol Bioeng. 2009;102(1):100–12." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d62726e793">9</a>]. Even though nutrient starvation has been reported to be the most suitable stimulant to raise lipid content [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ren HY, Liu BF, Ma C, Zhao L, Ren NQ. A new lipid-rich microalga Scenedesmus sp. strain R-16 isolated using Nile red staining: effects of carbon and nitrogen sources and initial pH on the biomass and lipid production. Biotechnol Biofuels. 2013;6(1):143." href="#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d62726e796">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Mata MT, Melo AC, Meireles S, Mendes AM, Martins AA, Caetano NS. Potential of microalgae Scenedesmus obliquus grown in brewery wastewater for biodiesel production. Chem Eng Trans. 2013;32:901–5." href="#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d62726e796_1">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wong YK, Yung KKL, Tsang YF, Xia Y, Wang L, Ho KC. Scenedesmus quadricauda for nutrient removal and lipid production in wastewater. Water Environ Res. 2015;87(12):2037–44." href="#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d62726e796_2">6</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Dasgupta CN, Suseela MR, Mandotra SK, Kumar P, Pandey MK, Toppo K, et al. Dual uses of microalgal biomass: an integrative approach for biohydrogen and biodiesel production. Appl Energy. 2015;146:202–8." href="#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d62726e796_3">7</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Knothe G. Improving biodiesel fuel properties by modifying fatty ester composition. Energy Environ Sci. 2009;2(7):759–66." href="#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d62726e796_4">8</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Rodolfi L, Chini Zittelli G, Bassi N, Padovani G, Biondi N, Bonini G, et al. Microalgae for oil: strain selection, induction of lipid synthesis and outdoor mass cultivation in a low-cost photobioreactor. Biotechnol Bioeng. 2009;102(1):100–12." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d62726e799">9</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Radakovits R, Jinkerson RE, Fuerstenberg SI, Tae H, Settlage RE, Boore JL, et al. Draft genome sequence and genetic transformation of the oleaginous alga Nannochloropsis gaditana. Nat Commun. 2012;3:e686." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d62726e802">18</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Bogen C, Al-Dilaimi A, Albersmeier A, Wichmann J, Grundmann M, Rupp O, et al. Reconstruction of the lipid metabolism for the microalga Monoraphidium neglectum from its genome sequence reveals characteristics suitable for biofuel production. BMC Genomics. 2013;14(1):e926." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d62726e805">22</a>], it is difficult to maintain nutrient deficient environment for large scale cultivation in open ponds. Moreover, in nutrient starvation model, although the lipid content increases, but it significantly reduces algal growth thus, affecting biomass content [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Knothe G. Improving biodiesel fuel properties by modifying fatty ester composition. Energy Environ Sci. 2009;2(7):759–66." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d62726e808">8</a>]. Thereby, we have aimed to identify high lipid yielding algae without any starvation and stress.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-1" data-title="Fig. 1"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig1" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 1</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4/figures/1" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1186%2Fs13068-018-1308-4/MediaObjects/13068_2018_1308_Fig1_HTML.png?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-1-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1186%2Fs13068-018-1308-4/MediaObjects/13068_2018_1308_Fig1_HTML.png" alt="figure1" loading="lazy" width="685" height="753" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-1-desc"><p>Comparison of <b>a</b> biomass productivity (g L<sup>−1</sup> day<sup>−1</sup>) and <b>b</b> lipid productivity (mg L<sup>−1</sup> day<sup>−1</sup>) of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 with other eight isolated oleaginous microalgae grown in autotrophic cultivation condition using BBM and mixotrophic cultivation condition using TAP media where acetate is supplemented as external carbon source in uniform cultivation condition at a temperature of 27 °C ± 0.5 °C, a photoperiod of 14:10 h light/dark cycle and fluorescent illumination of 3000 lux. [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Chiu SY, Kao CY, Tsai MT, Ong SC, Chen CH, Lin CS. Cultivation, photobioreactor design and harvesting of microalgae for biodiesel production: a critical review. Bioresour Technol. 2011;102(1):71–81." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d62726e943">24</a>]. As compared, <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 (biomass productivity 0.37 g L<sup>−1</sup> day<sup>−1</sup> and lipid productivity 102 mg L<sup>−1</sup> day<sup>−1</sup>) is on the higher side of the range (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig1">1</a>c) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Rodolfi L, Chini Zittelli G, Bassi N, Padovani G, Biondi N, Bonini G, et al. Microalgae for oil: strain selection, induction of lipid synthesis and outdoor mass cultivation in a low-cost photobioreactor. Biotechnol Bioeng. 2009;102(1):100–12." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d62726e962">9</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Santos RV, Dantas EL, de Oliveira CG, de Alvarenga CJ, dos Anjos CW, Guimarães EM, et al. J S Am Earth Sci. 2009;28(1):14–24." href="#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d62726e965">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Mandal S, Mallick N. Biodiesel production by the green microalga Scenedesmus obliquus in a recirculatory aquaculture system. Appl Microbiol Biotechnol. 2009;84:281–91." href="#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d62726e965_1">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yoo C, Jun SY, Lee JY, Ahn CY, Oh HM. Selection of microalgae for lipid production under high levels carbon dioxide. Bioresour Technol. 2010;101(1):S71–4." href="#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d62726e965_2">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Chiu SY, Kao CY, Tsai MT, Ong SC, Chen CH, Lin CS. Lipid accumulation and CO2 utilization of Nannochloropsis oculata in response to CO2 aeration. Bioresour Technol. 2009;100(2):833–8." href="#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d62726e965_3">28</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Liang Y, Sarkany N, Cui Y. Biomass and lipid productivities of Chlorella vulgaris under autotrophic, heterotrophic and mixotrophic growth conditions. Biotechnol Lett. 2009;31(7):1043–9." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d62726e968">29</a>]. Under large scale production, many studies have estimated the maximum productivity of algal biofuels ranges from 8.2 to 136.9 TOE ha<sup>−1</sup> year<sup>−1</sup> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Quinn JC, Catton K, Wagner N, Bradley TH. Current large-scale US biofuel potential from microalgae cultivated in photobioreactors. BioEnergy Res. 2012;5(1):49–60." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d62726e975">30</a>]. In some cases, the data from lab scale experiments are used to estimate the productivity of large scale production whereas some are real large scale production values. Our laboratory productivity numbers of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 have been extrapolated and found to be on higher side compared to other large-scale biofuel production platforms and are higher than the global average productivity (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig1">1</a>d) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Chisti Y. Biodiesel from microalgae. Biotechnol Adv. 2007;25:294–306." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d62726e985">1</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Park H, Lee C. Theoretical calculations on the feasibility of microalgal biofuels: utilization of marine resources could help realizing the potential of microalgae. Biotechnol J. 2016;11(11):1461–70." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d62726e988">11</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Radakovits R, Jinkerson RE, Fuerstenberg SI, Tae H, Settlage RE, Boore JL, et al. Draft genome sequence and genetic transformation of the oleaginous alga Nannochloropsis gaditana. Nat Commun. 2012;3:e686." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d62726e991">18</a>].</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec4">Fatty acid profile and biodiesel properties of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611</h3><p>The fatty acid profile of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 was found to be simple as compared to other known oleaginous algae, as it contains only six fatty acids (FA) of carbon chain length C16–C18 such as palmitic acid (16:0) 44.46%, oleic acid (18:1) 12.37%, linoleic acid (18:2) 11.29% and linolenic acid (18:3) 10.95% (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig1">1</a>d). According to EN14214, the percentage of linolenic acid (C18:3) and highly polyunsaturated FAs (≥ 4 double bond) in the biodiesel should not exceed the maximum limit of 12% and 1%, respectively [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="Dasgupta CN, Suseela MR, Mandotra SK, Kumar P, Pandey MK, Toppo K, et al. Dual uses of microalgal biomass: an integrative approach for biohydrogen and biodiesel production. Appl Energy. 2015;146:202–8." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1012">7</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Lang I, Hodac L, Friedl T, Feussner I. Fatty acid profiles and their distribution patterns in microalgae: a comprehensive analysis of more than 2000 strains from the SAG culture collection. BMC Plant Boil. 2011;11(1):e124." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1015">31</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Knothe G. Structure indices in FA chemistry How relevant is the iodine value? J Am Oil Chem Soc. 2002;79(9):847–54." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1018">32</a>]. In the present study, the percentage of linolenic acid was found to be 10.9% while polyunsaturated FAs with ≥ 4 double bond were completely absent, thus making it desirable for biodiesel production (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig1">1</a>d). The fatty acid methyl ester (FAME) profile of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 was compared with other two oleaginous algae such as <i>N. gaditana</i> CCMP526 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Radakovits R, Jinkerson RE, Fuerstenberg SI, Tae H, Settlage RE, Boore JL, et al. Draft genome sequence and genetic transformation of the oleaginous alga Nannochloropsis gaditana. Nat Commun. 2012;3:e686." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1031">18</a>] and <i>M. neglectum</i> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Bogen C, Al-Dilaimi A, Albersmeier A, Wichmann J, Grundmann M, Rupp O, et al. Reconstruction of the lipid metabolism for the microalga Monoraphidium neglectum from its genome sequence reveals characteristics suitable for biofuel production. BMC Genomics. 2013;14(1):e926." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1037">22</a>] whose genome was known and already been characterized for biofuel production. <i>N. gaditana</i> CCMP526, the high abundance of palmitic acid was observed along with an abundance of myristic acid (C14:0) as well as C16 unsaturated fatty acids, which were not detected in <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Radakovits R, Jinkerson RE, Fuerstenberg SI, Tae H, Settlage RE, Boore JL, et al. Draft genome sequence and genetic transformation of the oleaginous alga Nannochloropsis gaditana. Nat Commun. 2012;3:e686." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1047">18</a>]. In comparison, <i>M. neglectum</i> showed the high abundance of oleic acid (C18:1) and low abundance of saturated acids [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Bogen C, Al-Dilaimi A, Albersmeier A, Wichmann J, Grundmann M, Rupp O, et al. Reconstruction of the lipid metabolism for the microalga Monoraphidium neglectum from its genome sequence reveals characteristics suitable for biofuel production. BMC Genomics. 2013;14(1):e926." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1053">22</a>].</p><p>The biodiesel properties of FAME of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 were found to be within the limits of European standard EN14214 and EN 590:2013 (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Tab1">1</a>) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Standard B. EN 14214. European Standard Organization; 2003." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1065">33</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="European Committee for Standardization (CEN). EN 590: 2013. Automotive fuels—diesel—requirements and test methods. 2013." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1068">34</a>]. The FAMEs of <i>S. quadricauda</i> exhibits very less unsaturation and all the indices related to unsaturation such as degree of unsaturation (DU), iodine value (IV), allylic position equivalent (APE) and the bisallylic position equivalent (BAPE) were found to be within the range of EN14214 and EN 590:2013 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Standard B. EN 14214. European Standard Organization; 2003." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1075">33</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="European Committee for Standardization (CEN). EN 590: 2013. Automotive fuels—diesel—requirements and test methods. 2013." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1078">34</a>] (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Tab1">1</a>). The combustion quality indices cetane number (CN), higher heating value (HHV) and saponification value were also within the limits [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Knothe G. Fuel properties of highly polyunsaturated fatty acid methyl esters. Prediction of fuel properties of algal biodiesel. Energy Fuels. 2012;26(8):5265–73." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1084">35</a>] (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Tab1">1</a>). Another bottleneck of biofuel is inferior cold flow properties characterized by cloud point (CP), pour point (PP), cold filter plugging point (CFPP) and viscosity (<i>υ</i>) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Verma P, Sharma MP, Dwivedi G. Evaluation and enhancement of cold flow properties of palm oil and its biodiesel. Energy Rep. 2016;2:8–13." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1094">36</a>] (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Tab1">1</a>). Use of a fuel in colder regions depends upon its cold flow properties. Cold flow properties of FAMEs obtained were well within the accepted range of standard fuels. The CP and PP was obtained as 17 °C and 11.7 °C respectively that indicates biodiesel obtained from <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 will become cloudy and semisolid at the respective temperatures. Furthermore, cold filter plugging point (CFPP), the most important parameter for cold flow properties was obtained as 1.3 °C, which indicates the lowest temperature for free flowing fuel systems. The kinetic viscosity value (<i>υ</i>) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Knothe G, Steidley KR. Kinematic viscosity of biodiesel fuel components and related compounds. Influence of compound structure and comparison to petrodiesel fuel components. Fuel. 2005;84(9):1059–65." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1106">37</a>] and fuel density (<i>ρ</i>) are also strongly influenced by temperature [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Kolev SK, Petkov PS, Rangelov MA, Vayssilov GN. Density functional study of hydrogen bond formation between methanol and organic molecules containing Cl, F, NH2, OH, and COOH functional groups. J Phys Chem A. 2011;115(48):14054–68." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1113">38</a>] (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Tab1">1</a>).</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-1"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab1" data-test="table-caption">Table 1 Comparison of biodiesel properties of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 with standards of biodiesel and petro-diesel</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4/tables/1"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div>
<h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec5">Genome sequencing, draft assembly, functional annotation and comparative genomics of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611</h3><p>Although, <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 is a high biomass and lipid yielding microalgae, the production level is still a crucial criteria to make it possible candidate for economically sustainable biofuel production [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Shurin JB, Burkart MD, Mayfield SP, Smith VH. Recent progress and future challenges in algal biofuel production. F1000Res. 2016; e5." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1611">15</a>]. Thus molecular and genetic modifications to improve fatty acid contents or yield of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 are desired.</p><p>We are reporting for the first time whole genome sequencing of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 followed by de novo and reference assisted assembly with currently available tools and databases (Additional files <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#MOESM1">1</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#MOESM2">2</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#MOESM3">3</a>). Genome sequencing was performed using Ion Torrent Next-Generation Sequencing Technology (NGS) where a total of 57.27 million reads were obtained for further analysis (Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#MOESM1">1</a>). A complete set of 13,514 functional genes were identified from de novo assembly (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Tab2">2</a>). After cleaning, the reads were processed for reference mapping with <i>M. neglectum</i> (NCBI accession no NW_014013625.1 with genome size of 69.71 Mb), a closely related species of Chlorophyceae. 83.85% of the reads mapped to reference and the genome size recovered was 65.35 Mb, indicating a &gt; 90% genomic coverage. Further, to identify gene similarity with other algae, the annotated genes were processed for gene ontology in UniprotKB with 16,739 genes identified [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Bogen C, Al-Dilaimi A, Albersmeier A, Wichmann J, Grundmann M, Rupp O, et al. Reconstruction of the lipid metabolism for the microalga Monoraphidium neglectum from its genome sequence reveals characteristics suitable for biofuel production. BMC Genomics. 2013;14(1):e926." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d62726e1642">22</a>]. Reference-guided assembly has been reviewed in NCBI BioProject and assigned accession number NNCB00000000. The statistics pertaining to bioinformatics assembly are tabulated in Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Tab2">2</a>.</p><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-2"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab2" data-test="table-caption">Table 2 De novo genome assembly and reference-guided assembly statistics of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4/tables/2"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>The unavailability of the genomic sequence of <i>S. quadricauda</i> hampers the development of a more commercially viable strain, thus this attempt to elucidate its whole genome. The genome is currently in “draft assembly” stage as all the genes of its genome could not be identified by currently available tools and data bases. Based on the de novo and reference-assisted approach, although more than 90% of its genome information could be identified, still there are gaps in the assembly. One of the main reasons behind was the unavailability of closely related algal genome data to compare and authenticate the assembly. With the advancement of genome sequencing tools and platforms as well as continuous availability of novel genome information, all the gaps will be identified in future.</p><p>Based on annotation from de novo assembly, <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 belongs to empire Eukaryota, sub-kingdom Viridiplantae, phylum Chlorophyta, class Chlorophyceae and order Sphaeropleales (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig2">2</a>a). To resolve the anomaly, small subunit ribosomal RNA marker gene (18S rRNA) based identification was carried to identify the organism. The sequence of 18S rRNA gene was submitted to NCBI gene bank (accession no. KY654954), which demonstrated 99% similarity with partial sequence of <i>Desmodesmus intermedius</i> strain NMX451 18S rRNA gene (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig2">2</a>c). The holotype species of <i>Desmodesmus</i> is <i>Scenedesmus quadricauda</i> (Turpin) Brébisson (Algaebase) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Guiry MD. AlgaeBase. World-wide electronic publication; 2013. &#xA;                    http://www.algaebase.org&#xA;                    &#xA;                  ." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d62726e2543">39</a>]. A phylogenetic relationship was drawn on the basis of 18S rDNA sequence and NCBI blast. It was mostly clustered with different strains of <i>Desmodesmus</i> and <i>Scenedesmus</i> (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig2">2</a>c). Further, morphological characterization was carried out to confirm the identification of the organism (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig2">2</a>b) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Philipose MT. Chlorococcales. New Delhi: Indian Council of Agricultural Research; 1967." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d62726e2559">40</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Gupta RK. Algal flora of Dehradun district, Uttaranchal. Kolkata: Botanical Survey of Kolkata; 2005." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d62726e2562">41</a>]. The sample of <i>S. quadricauda</i> is preserved in CSIR-National Botanical Research Institute herbarium with accession number LWG002611 and germplasm is being maintained. The insufficient availability of DNA sequencing data is one of the major bottlenecks of DNA based taxonomy [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Huelsenbeck JP, Bull JJ, Cunningham CW. Combining data in phylogenetic analysis. Trends Ecol Evol. 1996;11(4):152–8." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d62726e2568">42</a>], thus further validation through morphological analysis is required [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Gregory TR. DNA barcoding does not compete with taxonomy. Nature. 2005;434:1067." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d62726e2571">43</a>].</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-2" data-title="Fig. 2"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig2" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 2</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" using Uniprot hits from Cellular component of the algae families and species. <b>b</b> Photomicrograph of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 under light microscope (×63). <b>c</b> Phylogenetic class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4/figures/2" data-track-dest="link:Figure2 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec6">Comparative analysis of predicted gene function and reconstruction of bioenergy metabolic pathways</h3><p>Investigation of metabolic pathways of interest and identification of bottlenecks for production are the major concerns of this work. The majority of <i>S. quadricauda</i> genes were present in catalytic activity, binding, metabolic processes, lipid metabolism and lipid biosynthetic processes. A total of 6167 genes were identified for cellular component in gene ontology terms (GOs), 6558 for biological processes, 8348 for molecular functions and 283 for lipid metabolism, amongst them some genes are common in all processes (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig3">3</a>a–d, Additional files <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#MOESM4">4</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#MOESM5">5</a>). Furthermore, special emphasis was laid on lipid metabolic pathway genes that are involved in lipid biosynthesis, TAG assembly and lipid catabolism (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig3">3</a>d). The genes involved in lipid metabolism were categorized in cellular lipid metabolic process and consisted of 127 genes, 111 genes were identified for lipid biosynthesis process and 33 genes were identified in lipid catabolism (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig3">3</a>d). Similarly, for glycolipid metabolism seven genes were identified while only 5 were identified for steroid metabolic process (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig3">3</a>d). The total gene numbers of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 was compared with <i>N. gaditana, M. neglectum</i> and <i>C. reinhardtii</i> (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#Fig3">3</a>e). It demonstrated larger number of genes annotated for overall catalytic activity (4442), binding activity (3049), overall metabolic process (2142), lipid metabolic process (127) and lipid biosynthetic process (111) (The Gene ontology of <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 is given in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#MOESM5">5</a>). Genome sizes of <i>N. gaditana</i>, <i>M. neglectum</i> and <i>C. reinhardtii</i> were reported as 29 Mb, 69.71 Mb and 120 Mb encoding 9052, 16,761, 17,743 protein coding genes respectively [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Radakovits R, Jinkerson RE, Fuerstenberg SI, Tae H, Settlage RE, Boore JL, et al. Draft genome sequence and genetic transformation of the oleaginous alga Nannochloropsis gaditana. Nat Commun. 2012;3:e686." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d62726e2664">18</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Merchant SS, Prochnik SE, Vallon O, Harris EH, Karpowicz SJ, Witman GB, et al. The Chlamydomonas genome reveals the evolution of key animal and plant functions. Science. 2007;318(5848):245–50." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d62726e2668">21</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Bogen C, Al-Dilaimi A, Albersmeier A, Wichmann J, Grundmann M, Rupp O, et al. Reconstruction of the lipid metabolism for the microalga Monoraphidium neglectum from its genome sequence reveals characteristics suitable for biofuel production. BMC Genomics. 2013;14(1):e926." href="/articles/10.1186/s13068-018-1308-4#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d62726e2671">22</a>]. This higher abundance of genes in <i>S. quadricauda</i> LWG002611 is reflecting in a larger regulatory and metabolic repertoire which could lead to high lipid accumulation in <i>S. quadricauda</i>. However, detailed functional investigation and transcriptome mapping are required to confirm the expression of gene families and to eliminate the pseudogenes.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-3" data-title="Fig. 3"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig3" class="c-article-section__figure-caption"
